*evaluationStateData) GetLocalValue(addr addrs.LocalValue, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n308: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n309: \n310: \t// First we'll make sure the requested value is declared in configuration,\n311: \t// so we can produce a nice message if not.\n312: \tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendantForInstance(d.ModulePath)\n313: \tif moduleConfig has no configuration\", d.ModulePath))\n317: \t}\n318: \n319: \tconfig := moduleConfig.Module.Locals[addr.Name]\n320: \tif config == nil {\n321: \t\tvar suggestions []string\n322: \t\tfor k := range {\n327: \t\t\tsuggestion = fmt.Sprintf(\" Did you mean %q?\", suggestion)\n328: \t\t}\n329: \n330: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n331: \t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n332: \t\t\tSummary: diags\n341: }\n342: \n343: func (d *evaluationStateData) GetModule(addr addrs.ModuleCall, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n344: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n345: \n346: \t// Output results live in the module that declares them, which is one of\n347: \t// the child module instances of our current module path.\n348: \tmoduleAddr := d.ModulePath.Module().Child(addr.Name)\n349: \tabsAddr := addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)\n350: \n351: \tparentCfg := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendantForInstance(d.ModulePath)\n352: \tcallConfig, ok := parentCfg.Module.ModuleCalls[addr.Name]\n353: \tif !ok {\n354: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n355: \t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n356: \t\t\tSummary:  `Reference to undeclared module`,\n357: \t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`The configuration contains no %s.`, moduleAddr),\n358: \t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n359: \t\t})\n360: \t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n361: \t}\n362: \n363: \t// We'll consult the configuration to see what output names we are\n364: \t// expecting, so we can ensure the resulting object is of the expected\n365: \t// type even if our data is incomplete for some reason.\n366: \tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.Descendant(moduleAddr)\n367: \tif moduleConfig == nil {\n368: \t\t// should never happen, since we have a valid module call above, this\n369: \t\t// should be caught during static validation.\n370: \t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"output value read from %s, which has no configuration\", moduleAddr))\n371: \t}\n372: \toutputConfigs := moduleConfig.Module.Outputs\n373: \n374: \t// We don't do instance expansion during validation, and so we need to\n375: \t// return an unknown value. Technically we should always return\n376: \t// cty.DynamicVal here because the final value during plan will always\n377: \t// be an object or tuple type with unpredictable attributes/elements,\n378: \t// but because we never actually carry values forward from validation to\n379: \t// planning we lie a little here and return unknown list and map types,\n380: \t// just to give us more opportunities to catch author mistakes during\n381: \t// validation.\n382: \t//\n383: \t// This means that in practice any expression that refers to a module\n384: \t// call must be written to be valid for either a collection type or\n385: \t// structural type of similar kind, so that it can be considered as\n386: \t// valid during both the validate and plan walks.\n387: \tif d.Operation == walkValidate {\n388: \t\tatys := make(map[string]cty.Type, len(outputConfigs))\n389: \t\tfor name := range outputConfigs {\n390: \t\t\tatys[name] = cty.DynamicPseudoType // output values are dynamically-typed\n391: \t\t}\n392: \t\tinstTy := cty.Object(atys)\n393: \n394: \t\tswitch {\n395: \t\tcase callConfig.Count != nil:\n396: \t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cty.List(instTy)), diags\n397: \t\tcase callConfig.ForEach != nil:\n398: \t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cty.Map(instTy)), diags\n399: \t\tdefault:\n400: \t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(instTy), diags\n401: \t\t}\n402: \t}\n403: \n404: \t// For all other walk types, we proceed to dynamic evaluation of individual\n405: \t// instances, using the global instance expander. An earlier graph node\n406: \t// should always have registered the expansion of this module call before\n407: \t// we get here, unless there's a bug in the graph builders.\n408: \tallInstances := d.Evaluator.Instances\n409: \tinstKeyType, instKeys, known := allInstances.ExpandAbsModuleCall(absAddr)\n410: \tif !known {\n411: \t\t// If we don't know which instances exist then we can't really predict\n412: \t\t// anything at all. We can't even predict the return type based on\n413: \t\t// instKeyType because output values are dynamically-typed and so\n414: \t\t// our final result will always be an object or tuple type whose\n415: \t\t// attribute/element count we cannot predict.\n416: \t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n417: \t}\n418: \n419: \tinstanceObjVal := func(instKey addrs.InstanceKey) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n420: \t\t// This function must always return a valid value, even if it's\n421: \t\t// just a cty.DynamicVal placeholder accompanying error diagnostics.\n422: \t\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n423: \n424: \t\tnamedVals := d.Evaluator.NamedValues\n425: \t\tmoduleInstAddr := absAddr.Instance(instKey)\n426: \t\tattrs := make(map[string]cty.Value, len(outputConfigs))\n427: \t\tfor name := range outputConfigs {\n428: \t\t\toutputAddr := moduleInstAddr.OutputValue(name)\n429: \n430: \t\t\t// Although we do typically expect the graph dependencies to\n431: \t\t\t// ensure that values get registered before they are needed,\n432: \t\t\t// we track depedencies with specific output values where\n433: \t\t\t// possible, instead of with entire module calls, and so\n434: \t\t\t// in this specific case it's valid for some of this call's\n435: \t\t\t// output values to not be known yet, with the graph builder\n436: \t\t\t// being responsible for making sure that no expression\n437: \t\t\t// in the configuration can actually observe that.\n438: \t\t\tif !namedVals.HasOutputValue(outputAddr) {\n439: \t\t\t\tattrs[name] = cty.DynamicVal\n440: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n441: \t\t\t}\n442: \t\t\toutputVal := namedVals.GetOutputValue(outputAddr)\n443: \t\t\tattrs[name] = outputVal\n444: \t\t}\n445: \n446: \t\treturn cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n447: \t}\n448: \n449: \tswitch instKeyType {\n450: \n451: \tcase addrs.NoKeyType:\n452: \t\t// In this case we should always have exactly one instance that\n453: \t\t// is addrs.NoKey. If not then there's a bug in the [instances.Expander]\n454: \t\t// implementation.\n455: \t\tif len(instKeys) != 1 {\n456: \t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"module call has no instance key type but has %d instances (should be 1)\", len(instKeys)))\n457: \t\t}\n458: \t\tret, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKeys[0])\n459: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n460: \t\treturn ret, diags\n461: \n462: \tcase addrs.IntKeyType:\n463: \t\t// We can assume that the instance keys are in ascending numerical order\n464: \t\t// and are consecutive, per the contract of allInstances.ExpandModuleCall.\n465: \t\telems := make([]cty.Value, 0, len(instKeys))\n466: \t\tfor _, instKey := range instKeys {\n467: \t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKey)\n468: \t\t\telems = append(elems, instVal)\n469: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n470: \t\t}\n471: \t\treturn cty.TupleVal(elems), diags\n472: \n473: \tcase addrs.StringKeyType:\n474: \t\tattrs := make(map[string]cty.Value, len(instKeys))\n475: \t\tfor _, instKey := range instKeys {\n476: \t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKey)\n477: \t\t\tattrs[string(instKey.(addrs.StringKey))] = instVal\n478: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n479: \t\t}\n480: \t\treturn cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n481: \n482: \tdefault:\n483: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n484: \t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n485: \t\t\tSummary:  `Unsupported instance key type`,\n486: \t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n487: \t\t\t\t`Module call %s has instance key type %#v, which is not supported by the expression evaluator. This is a bug in Terraform.`,\n488: \t\t\t\tabsAddr, instKeyType,\n489: \t\t\t),\n490: \t\t\tSubject: rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n491: \t\t})\n492: \t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n493: \t}\n494: }\n495: \n496: func (d *evaluationStateData) GetResource(addr addrs.Resource, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n497: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n498: \t// First we'll consult the configuration to see if an resource of this\n499: \t// name is declared at all.\n500: \tmoduleAddr := d.ModulePath\n501: \tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendantForInstance(moduleAddr)\n502: \tif moduleConfig == nil {\n503: \t\t// should never happen, since we can't be evaluating in a module\n504: \t\t// that wasn't mentioned in configuration.\n505: \t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"resource value read from %s, which has no configuration\", moduleAddr))\n506: \t}\n507: \n508: \tconfig := moduleConfig.Module.ResourceByAddr(addr)\n509: \tif config == nil {\n510: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n511: \t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n512: \t\t\tSummary:  `Reference to undeclared resource`,\n513: \t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`A \t}\n518: \n519: \t// Much of this function was written before we had factored out the handling\n520: \t// of instance keys into the separate instance expander model, and so it\n521: \t// does a bunch of instance-related work itself below.\n522: \t//\n523: \t// Currently, unknown instance keys are only possible when planning with\n524: \t// DeferralAllowed set to true in the PlanOpts, which should stacks-specific behaviors won't leak out into the standard\n528: \t// runtime.\n529: \t//\n530: \t// TODO: When deferred actions are more stable and robust in stacks, it\n531: \t// would be nice to rework this function to rely on the ResourceInstanceKeys\n532: \t// result for _all_ of its work, rather than continuing to duplicate a bunch\n533: \t// of the logic we've tried to encapsulate over can't even predict what the result type will be because it\n539: \t\t\t// would be either an object or tuple type decided based on the instance\n540: \t\t\t// keys.\n541: \t\t\t// (We can't get in here for a single-instance resource because in that\n542: \t\t\t// case we would know that there's only one key and it's addrs.NoKey,\n543: \t\t\t// so we'll fall through to the other logic below.)\n544: \t\t\tunknownVal := cty.DynamicVal\n545: \n546: \t\t\t// If an ephemeral resource is deferred we need to mark the returned unknown value as ephemeral\n547: \t\t\tif addr.Mode == addrs.EphemeralResourceMode {\n548: \t\t\t\tunknownVal = unknownVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral)\n549: \t\t\t}\n550: \t\t\treturn unknownVal, diags\n551: \t\t}\n552: \t}\n553: \n554: \t// Build the provider address from configuration, since we may not have\n555: \t// state available in all cases.\n556: \t// We need to build an abs provider address, but we can use a default\n557: \t// instance since we're only interested in the schema.\n558: \tschema := d.getResourceSchema(addr, config.Provider)\n559: \tif schema == nil {\n560: \t\t// This shouldn't happen, since validation before we get here should've\n561: \t\t// taken care of it, but we'll show a reasonable error message anyway.\n562: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n563: \t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n564: \t\t\tSummary:  `Missing resource type schema`,\n565: \t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"No schema is available for %s in %s. This is a bug in Terraform and should be reported.\", addr, config.Provider),\n566: \t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n567: \t\t})\n568: \t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n569: \t}\n570: \tty := schema.ImpliedType()\n571: \n572: \tif addr.Mode == addrs.EphemeralResourceMode {\n573: \t\t// FIXME: This does not yet work with deferrals, and it would be nice to\n574: \t\t// find some way to refactor this so that the following code is not so\n575: \t\t// tethered to the current implementation details. Instead we should\n576: \t\t// have an abstract idea of first determining what instances the\n577: \t\t// resource has (using d.Evaluator.Instances.ResourceInstanceKeys) and\n578: \t\t// then retrieving the value for each instance to assemble into the\n579: \t\t// result, using some per-resource-mode logic maintained elsewhere.\n580: \t\treturn d.getEphemeralResource(addr, rng)\n581: \t}\n582: \n583: \trs := d.Evaluator.State.Resource(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath))\n584: \n585: \tif rs == nil {\n586: \t\tswitch d.Operation {\n587: \t\tcase walkPlan, walkApply:\n588: \t\t\t// During plan and apply as we evaluate each removed instance they\n589: \t\t\t// are removed from the working state. Since we know there are no\n590: \t\t\t// instances, return an empty container of the expected type.\n591: \t\t\tswitch {\n592: \t\t\tcase config.Count != nil:\n593: \t\t\t\treturn cty.EmptyTupleVal, diags\n594: \t\t\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n595: \t\t\t\treturn cty.EmptyObjectVal, diags\n596: \t\t\tdefault:\n597: \t\t\t\t// While we can reference an expanded resource with 0\n598: \t\t\t\t// instances, we cannot reference instances that do not exist.\n599: \t\t\t\t// Due to the fact that we may have direct references to\n600: \t\t\t\t// instances that may end up in a root output during destroy\n601: \t\t\t\t// (since a planned destroy cannot yet remove root outputs), we\n602: \t\t\t\t// need to return a dynamic value here to allow evaluation to\n603: \t\t\t\t// continue.\n604: \t\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[ERROR] unknown instance %q referenced during %s\", addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath), d.Operation)\n605: \t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n606: \t\t\t}\n607: \n608: \t\tcase walkImport:\n609: \t\t\t// Import does not yet plan resource changes, so new resources from\n610: \t\t\t// config are not going to be found here. Once walkImport fully\n611: \t\t\t// plans resources, this case should not longer be needed.\n612: \t\t\t// In the single instance case, we can return a typed unknown value\n613: \t\t\t// for the instance to better satisfy other expressions using the\n614: \t\t\t// value. This of course will not help if statically known\n615: \t\t\t// attributes are expected to be known elsewhere, but reduces the\n616: \t\t\t// number of problematic configs for now.\n617: \t\t\t// Unlike in plan and apply above we can't be sure the count or\n618: \t\t\t// for_each instances are empty, so we return a DynamicVal. We\n619: \t\t\t// don't really have a good value to return otherwise -- empty\n620: \t\t\t// values will fail for direct index expressions, and unknown\n621: \t\t\t// Lists and Maps could fail in some type unifications.\n622: \t\t\tswitch {\n623: \t\t\tcase config.Count != nil:\n624: \t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n625: \t\t\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n626: \t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n627: \t\t\tdefault:\n628: \t\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(ty), diags\n629: \t\t\t}\n630: \n631: \t\tdefault:\n632: \t\t\t// We should only end up here during the validate walk (or\n633: \t\t\t// console/eval), since later walks should have at least partial\n634: \t\t\t// states populated for all resources in the configuration.\n635: \t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n636: \t\t}\n637: \t}\n638: \n639: \t// Now, we're going to build up a value that represents the resource\n640: \t// or resources that are in the state.\n641: \tinstances := map[addrs.InstanceKey]cty.Value{}\n642: \n643: \t// First, we're going to load any instances that we have written into the\n644: \t// deferrals system. A deferred resource overrides anything that might be\n645: \t// in the state for the resource, so we do this first.\n646: \tfor key, value := range d.Evaluator.Deferrals.GetDeferredResourceInstances(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)) {\n647: \t\tinstances[key] = value\n648: \t}\n649: \n650: \t// Decode all instances in the current state\n651: \tpendingDestroy := d.Operation == walkDestroy\n652: \tfor key, is := range rs.Instances {\n653: \t\tif _, ok := instances[key]; ok {\n654: \t\t\t// Then we've already loaded this instance from the deferrals so\n655: \t\t\t// we'll just ignore it being in state.\n656: \t\t\tcontinue\n657: \t\t}\n658: \t\t// Otherwise, we'll load the instance from state.\n659: \n660: \t\tif is == nil || is.Current == nil {\n661: \t\t\t// Assume we're dealing with an instance that hasn't been created yet.\n662: \t\t\tinstances[key] = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n663: \t\t\tcontinue\n664: \t\t}\n665: \n666: \t\tinstAddr := addr.Instance(key).Absolute(d.ModulePath)\n667: \t\tchange := d.Evaluator.Changes.GetResourceInstanceChange(instAddr, addrs.NotDeposed)\n668: \t\tif change != nil {\n669: \t\t\t// Don't take any resources that are yet to be deleted into account.\n670: \t\t\t// If the referenced resource is CreateBeforeDestroy, then orphaned\n671: \t\t\t// instances will be in the state, as they are not destroyed until\n672: \t\t\t// after their dependants are updated.\n673: \t\t\tif change.Action == plans.Delete {\n674: \t\t\t\tif !pendingDestroy {\n675: \t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n676: \t\t\t\t}\n677: \t\t\t}\n678: \t\t}\n679: \n680: \t\t// Planned resources are temporarily stored in state with empty values,\n681: \t\t// and need to be replaced by the planned value here.\n682: \t\tif is.Current.Status == states.ObjectPlanned {\n683: \t\t\tif change == nil {\n684: \t\t\t\t// FIXME: This is usually an unfortunate case where we need to\n685: \t\t\t\t// lookup an individual instance referenced via \"self\" for\n686: \t\t\t\t// postconditions which we know exists, but because evaluation\n687: \t\t\t\t// must always get the resource in aggregate some instance\n688: \t\t\t\t// changes may not yet be registered.\n689: \t\t\t\tinstances[key] = cty.DynamicVal\n690: \t\t\t\t// log the problem for debugging, since it may be a legitimate error we can't catch\n691: \t\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[WARN] instance %s is marked as having a change pending but that change is not recorded in the plan\", instAddr)\n692: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n693: \t\t\t}\n694: \t\t\tinstances[key] = change.After\n695: \t\t\tcontinue\n696: \t\t}\n697: \n698: \t\tios, err := is.Current.Decode(ty)\n699: \t\tif err != nil {\n700: \t\t\t// This shouldn't happen, since by the time we get here we\n701: \t\t\t// should have upgraded the state data already.\n702: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n703: \t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n704: \t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Invalid resource instance data in state\",\n705: \t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"Instance %s data could not be decoded from the state: %s.\", instAddr, err),\n706: \t\t\t\tSubject:  &config.DeclRange,\n707: \t\t\t})\n708: \t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t}\n710: \n711: \t\tval := ios.Value\n712: \n713: \t\tinstances[key] = val\n714: \t}\n715: \n716: \t// ret should be populated with a valid value in all cases below\n717: \tvar ret cty.Value\n718: \n719: \tswitch {\n720: \tcase config.Count != nil:\n721: \t\t// figure out what the last index we have is\n722: \t\tlength := -1\n723: \t\tfor key := range instances {\n724: \t\t\tintKey, ok := key.(addrs.IntKey)\n725: \t\t\tif !ok {\n726: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n727: \t\t\t}\n728: \t\t\tif int(intKey) >= length {\n729: \t\t\t\tlength = int(intKey) + 1\n730: \t\t\t}\n731: \t\t}\n732: \n733: \t\tif length > 0 {\n734: \t\t\tvals := make([]cty.Value, length)\n735: \t\t\tfor key, instance := range instances {\n736: \t\t\t\tintKey, ok := key.(addrs.IntKey)\n737: \t\t\t\tif !ok {\n738: \t\t\t\t\t// old key from state, which isn't valid for evaluation\n739: \t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n740: \t\t\t\t}\n741: \n742: \t\t\t\tvals[int(intKey)] = instance\n743: \t\t\t}\n744: \n745: \t\t\t// Insert unknown values where there are any missing instances\n746: \t\t\tfor i, v := range vals {\n747: \t\t\t\tif v == cty.NilVal {\n748: \t\t\t\t\tvals[i] = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n749: \t\t\t\t}\n750: \t\t\t}\n751: \t\t\tret = cty.TupleVal(vals)\n752: \t\t} else {\n753: \t\t\tret = cty.EmptyTupleVal\n754: \t\t}\n755: \n756: \tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n757: \t\tvals := make(map[string]cty.Value)\n758: \t\tfor key, instance := range instances {\n759: \t\t\tstrKey, ok := key.(addrs.StringKey)\n760: \t\t\tif !ok {\n761: \t\t\t\t// old key that is being dropped and not used for evaluation\n762: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n763: \t\t\t}\n764: \t\t\tvals[string(strKey)] = instance\n765: \t\t}\n766: \n767: \t\tif len(vals) > 0 {\n768: \t\t\t// We use an object rather than a map \t\t\t// though they all conform to the static schema.\n772: \t\t\tret = cty.ObjectVal(vals)\n773: \t\t} else {\n774: \t\t\tret = cty.EmptyObjectVal\n775: \t\t}\n776: \n777: \tdefault:\n778: \t\tval, \t}\n786: \n787: \treturn ret, diags\n788: }\n789: \n790: func (d *evaluationStateData) getEphemeralResource(addr addrs.Resource, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n791: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n792: \n793: \tif d.Operation == walkValidate || d.Operation == walkEval {\n794: \t\t// Ephemeral instances are never live during the validate walk. Eval is\n795: \t\t// similarly offline, and since there is no value stored we can't return\n796: \t\t// anything other than dynamic.\n797: \t\treturn cty.DynamicVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral), diags\n798: \t}\n799: \n800: \t// Now, we're going to build up a value that represents the resource\n801: \t// or resources that are in the state.\n802: \tinstances := map[addrs.InstanceKey]cty.Value{}\n803: \n804: \t// First, we're going to load any instances that we have written into the\n805: \t// deferrals system. A deferred resource overrides anything that might be\n806: \t// in the state for the resource, so we do this first.\n807: \tfor key, value := range d.Evaluator.Deferrals.GetDeferredResourceInstances(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)) {\n808: \t\tinstances[key] = value\n809: \t}\n810: \n811: \tabsAddr := addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)\n812: \tkeyType, keys, haveUnknownKeys := d.Evaluator.Instances.ResourceInstanceKeys(absAddr)\n813: \tif haveUnknownKeys {\n814: \t\t// We can probably do better than totally unknown at least for a\n815: \t\t// single-instance resource, but we'll just keep it simple for now.\n816: \t\t// Result must be marked as ephemeral so that we can still catch\n817: \t\t// attempts to use the results in non-ephemeral locations, so that\n818: \t\t// the operator doesn't end up trapped with an error on a subsequent\n819: \t\t// plan/apply round.\n820: \t\treturn cty.DynamicVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral), diags\n821: \t}\n822: \n823: \tephems := d.Evaluator.EphemeralResources\n824: \tgetInstValue := func(addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n825: \t\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n826: \n827: \t\t// If we have a deferred instance with this key we don't need to check if it is live or not,\n828: \t\t// it has not been created so we can just return the deferred value.\n829: \t\tif v, ok := instances[addr.Resource.Key]; ok {\n830: \t\t\treturn v, diags\n831: \t\t}\n832: \n833: \t\tval, isLive := ephems.InstanceValue(addr)\n834: \t\tif !isLive {\n835: \t\t\t// If the instance is no longer \"live\" by the time we're accessing\n836: \t\t\t// it then that suggests that it needed renewal and renewal has\n837: \t\t\t// failed, and so the object's value is no longer usable. depended on the liveness of this object.\n841: \t\t\t//\n842: \t\t\t// This error message is written on the assumption that it will\n843: \t\t\t// always appear alongside the provider's renewal error, times.\n847: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n848: \t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n849: \t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Ephemeral resource instance has expired\",\n850: \t\t\t\tDetail: \t\t\t\tSubject: rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n855: \t\t\t})\n856: \t\t}\n857: \t\tif val == cty.NilVal {\n858: \t\t\tval = cty.DynamicVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral)\n859: \t\t}\n860: \t\treturn val, diags\n861: \t}\n862: \n863: \tswitch keyType {\n864: \tcase addrs.NoKeyType:\n865: \t\t// For \"no key\" we're returning just a single object representing\n866: \t\t// the single instance of this resource.\n867: \t\tinstVal, moreDiags := getInstValue(absAddr.Instance(addrs.NoKey))\n868: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n869: \t\treturn instVal, diags\n870: \tcase addrs.IntKeyType:\n871: \t\t// For integer cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n894: \tdefault:\n895: \t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"unhandled instance key type %#v\", keyType))\n896: \t}\n897: }\n898: \n899: func (d *evaluationStateData) This\\n195: \\t\\t// is a useful simplification so that module authors can be explicit\\n196: \\t\\t// about what guarantees they are intending to make (regardless of\\n197: \\t\\t// current implementation details). This is just here for robustness.\\n210: \\t\\t\\t\\tsubject = cfg.DeclRange\\n211: \\t\\t\\t}\\n212: \\n213: \\t\\t\\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\\n214: \\t\\t\\t\\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\\n215: \\t\\t\\t\\tSummary:  \\\"Ephemeral value not allowed\\\",\\n216: \\t\\t\\t\\tDetail:   \\\"This input variable is not declared as accepting a ephemeral values, so it cannot be set to a result derived from an ephemeral value.\\\",\\n217: \\t\\t\\t\\tSubject:  subject.Ptr(),\\n218: \\t\\t\\t})\\n219: \\t\\t}\\n220: \\t}\\n221: \\n222: \\treturn val, diags\\n223: }\\n224: \\n225: // evalVariableValidations ensures that all of the configured custom validations\\n226: // for a variable are passing.\\n227: //\\n228: // This must be used only after any side-effects that make the value of the\\n229: // variable available for use in expression evaluation, such as\\n230: // EvalModuleCallArgument for variables in descendant modules.\\n231: func evalVariableValidations(addr addrs.AbsInputVariableInstance, ctx EvalContext, rules []*configs.CheckRule, valueRng hcl.Range, validateWalk bool) (diags tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\\n232: \\tif len(rules) == 0 {\\n233: \\t\\tlog.Printf(\\\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: no validation rules declared for %s, so skipping\\\", addr)\\n234: \\t\\treturn nil\\n235: \\t}\\n236: \\tlog.Printf(\\\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: validating %s\\\", addr)\\n237: \\n238: \\tcheckState := ctx.Checks()\\n239: \\tif !checkState.ConfigHasChecks(addr.ConfigCheckable()) {\\n240: \\t\\t// We have nothing to do if this object doesn't have any checks,\\n241: \\t\\t// but the \\\"rules\\\" slice should agree that we don't.\\n242: \\t\\tif ct := len(rules); ct != 0 {\\n243: \\t\\t\\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\\\"check state says that %s should have no rules, but it has %d\\\", addr, ct))\\n244: \\t\\t}\\n245: \\t\\treturn diags\\n246: \\t}\\n247: \\n248: \\t// We'll build just one evaluation context covering the data needed by\\n249: \\t// all of the rules together, since that'll minimize lock contention\\n250: \\t// on the state, plan, etc.\\n251: \\tscope := ctx.EvaluationScope(nil, nil, EvalDataForNoInstanceKey)\\n252: \\tvar refs []*addrs.Reference\\n253: \\tfor _, rule := range rules {\\n254: \\t\\tcondRefs, moreDiags := langrefs.ReferencesInExpr(addrs.ParseRef, rule.Condition)\\n255: \\t\\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\\n256: \\t\\tmsgRefs, moreDiags := langrefs.ReferencesInExpr(addrs.ParseRef, rule.ErrorMessage)\\n257: \\t\\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\\n258: \\t\\trefs = append(refs, condRefs...)\\n259: \\t\\trefs = append(refs, msgRefs...)\\n260: \\t}\\n261: \\tif diags.HasErrors() {\\n262: \\t\\t// If any of the references were invalid then evaluating the expressions\\n263: \\t\\t// will duplicate those errors, so we'll bail out early.\\n264: \\t\\treturn diags\\n265: \\t}\\n266: \\thclCtx, moreDiags := scope.EvalContext(refs)\\n267: \\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\\n268: \\tif moreDiags.HasErrors() {\\n269: \\t\\treturn diags\\n270: \\t}\\n271: \\n272: \\t// HACK: Historically we manually built a very constrained hcl.EvalContext\\n273: \\t// here, which only included the value of the one specific input variable\\n274: \\t// we're validating, since we didn't yet support referring to anything\\n275: \\t// else. ct != 0 {\n243: \t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"check state says that %s should have no rules, but it has %d\", addr, ct))\n244: \t\t}\n245: \t\treturn diags\n246: \t}\n247: \n248: \t// We'll build just one evaluation context covering the data needed by\n249: \t// all of the rules together, since that'll minimize lock contention\n250: \t// on the state, plan, etc.\n251: \tscope := ctx.EvaluationScope(nil, nil, EvalDataForNoInstanceKey)\n252: \tvar refs []*addrs.Reference\n253: \tfor _, rule := range rules {\n254: \t\tcondRefs, moreDiags := langrefs.ReferencesInExpr(addrs.ParseRef, rule.Condition)\n255: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n256: \t\tmsgRefs, moreDiags := langrefs.ReferencesInExpr(addrs.ParseRef, rule.ErrorMessage)\n257: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n258: \t\trefs = append(refs, condRefs...)\n259: \t\trefs = append(refs, msgRefs...)\n260: \t}\n261: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n262: \t\t// If any of the references were invalid then evaluating the expressions\n263: \t\t// will duplicate those errors, so we'll bail out early.\n264: \t\treturn diags\n265: \t}\n266: \thclCtx, moreDiags := scope.EvalContext(refs)\n267: \tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n268: \tif moreDiags.HasErrors() {\n269: \t\treturn diags\n270: \t}\n271: \n272: \t// HACK: Historically we manually built a very constrained hcl.EvalContext\n273: \t// here, which only included the value of the one specific input variable\n274: \t// we're validating, since we didn't yet support referring to anything\n275: \t// else. That accidentally bypassed our rule that input variables are\n276: \t// always unknown during the validate walk, and thus accidentally created\n277: \t// a useful behavior of actually checking constant-only values against\n278: \t// their validation rules just during \"terraform validate\", rather than\n279: \t// having to run \"terraform plan\".\n280: \t//\n281: \t// Although that behavior was accidental, it makes simple validation rules\n282: \t// more useful and is protected by compatibility promises, and so we'll\n283: \t// fake it here by overwriting the unknown value that scope.EvalContext\n284: \t// will have inserted with a possibly-more-known value using the same\n285: \t// strategy our special code used to use.\n286: \tourVal := ctx.NamedValues().GetInputVariableValue(addr)\n287: \tif ourVal != cty.NilVal {\n288: \t\t// (it would be weird for ourVal to be nil here, but we'll tolerate it\n289: \t\t// because it was scope.EvalContext's responsibility to check for the\n290: \t\t// absent final value, and even if it didn't we'll just get an\n291: \t\t// evaluation error when evaluating the expressions below anyway.)\n292: \n293: \t\t// Our goal here is to make sure that a reference to the variable\n294: \t\t// we're checking will evaluate to ourVal, regardless of what else\n295: \t\t// scope.EvalContext might have put in the variables table.\n296: \t\tif hclCtx.Variables == nil {\n297: \t\t\thclCtx.Variables = make(map[string]cty.Value)\n298: \t\t}\n299: \t\tif varsVal, ok := hclCtx.Variables[\"var\"]; ok {\n300: \t\t\t// Unfortunately we need to unpack and repack the object here,\n301: \t\t\t// because cty values are immutable.\n302: \t\t\tattrs := varsVal.AsValueMap()\n303: \t\t\tattrs[addr.Variable.Name] = ourVal\n304: \t\t\thclCtx.Variables[\"var\"] = cty.ObjectVal(attrs)\n305: \t\t} else {\n306: \t\t\thclCtx.Variables[\"var\"] = cty.ObjectVal(map[string]cty.Value{\n307: \t\t\t\taddr.Variable.Name: ourVal,\n308: \t\t\t})\n309: \t\t}\n310: \t}\n311: \n312: \tfor ix, validation := range rules {\n313: \t\tresult, ruleDiags := evalVariableValidation(validation, hclCtx, valueRng, addr, ix, validateWalk)\n314: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(ruleDiags)\n315: \n316: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: %s status is now %s\", addr, result.Status)\n317: \t\tif result.Status == checks.StatusFail {\n318: \t\t\tcheckState.ReportCheckFailure(addr, addrs.InputValidation, ix, result.FailureMessage)\n319: \t\t} else {\n320: \t\t\tcheckState.ReportCheckResult(addr, addrs.InputValidation, ix, result.Status)\n321: \t\t}\n322: \t}\n323: \n324: \treturn diags\n325: }\n326: \n327: func evalVariableValidation(validation *configs.CheckRule, hclCtx *hcl.EvalContext, valueRng hcl.Range, addr addrs.AbsInputVariableInstance, ix int, validateWalk bool) (checkResult, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n328: \tconst errInvalidCondition = \"Invalid variable validation result\"\n329: \tconst errInvalidValue = \"Invalid value for variable\"\n330: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n331: \n332: \tresult, moreDiags := validation.Condition.Value(hclCtx)\n333: \tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n334: \terrorValue, errorDiags := validation.ErrorMessage.Value(hclCtx)\n335: \n336: \t// The following error handling is a workaround to preserve backwards\n337: \t// compatibility. Due to an implementation quirk, all prior versions of\n338: \t// Terraform would treat error messages specified using JSON\n339: \t// configuration syntax (.tf.json) as string literals, even if they\n340: \t// contained the \"${\" template expression operator. This behaviour did\n341: \t// not match that of HCL configuration syntax, where a template\n342: \t// expression would result in a validation error.\n343: \t//\n344: \t// As a result, users writing or generating JSON configuration syntax\n345: \t// may have specified error messages which are invalid template\n346: \t// expressions. As we add support for error message expressions, we are\n347: \t// unable to perfectly distinguish between these two cases.\n348: \t//\n349: \t// To ensure that we don't break backwards compatibility, we have the\n350: \t// below fallback logic if the error message fails to evaluate. This\n351: \t// should only have any effect for JSON configurations. The gohcl\n352: \t// DecodeExpression function behaves differently when the source of the\n353: \t// expression is a JSON configuration file and a nil context is passed.\n354: \tif errorDiags.HasErrors() {\n355: \t\t// Attempt to decode the expression as a string literal. Please file a GitHub issue if this would break your workflow.\\n\\n%s\", errorDiags.Error()),\n374: \t\t\t\t\tSubject:     validation.ErrorMessage.Range().Ptr(),\n375: \t\t\t\t\tContext:     validation.DeclRange.Ptr(),\n376: \t\t\t\t\tExpression:  validation.ErrorMessage,\n377: \t\t\t\t\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\n378: \t\t\t\t},\n379: \t\t\t}\n380: \t\t}\n381: \n382: \t\t// We want to either report the original diagnostics if the\n383: \t\t// fallback failed, or the warning generated above if it succeeded.\n384: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(errorDiags)\n385: \t}\n386: \n387: \tif !result.IsKnown() {\n391: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: %s rule %s condition value is unknown, so skipping validation for now\", addr, validation.DeclRange)\n392: \n393: \t\treturn checkResult{Status: checks.StatusUnknown}, diags // We'll wait until we've learned more, then.\n394: \t}\n395: \tif result.IsNull() {\n396: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n397: \t\t\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagError,\n398: \t\t\tSummary:     errInvalidCondition,\n399: \t\t\tDetail:      \"Validation condition expression must return either true or false, not null.\",\n400: \t\t\tSubject:     validation.Condition.Range().Ptr(),\n401: \t\t\tExpression:  validation.Condition,\n402: \t\t\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\n403: \t\t})\n404: \t\treturn checkResult{Status: checks.StatusError}, diags\n405: \t}\n406: \tvar err error\n407: \tresult, err = convert.Convert(result, cty.Bool)\n408: \tif err != nil {\n409: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n410: \t\t\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagError,\n411: \t\t\tSummary:     errInvalidCondition,\n412: \t\t\tDetail:      fmt.Sprintf(\"Invalid validation condition result value: %s.\", tfdiags.FormatError(err)),\n413: \t\t\tSubject:     validation.Condition.Range().Ptr(),\n414: \t\t\tExpression:  validation.Condition,\n415: \t\t\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\n416: \t\t})\n417: \t\treturn checkResult{Status: checks.StatusError}, diags\n418: \t}\n419: \n420: \t// Validation condition may be marked if the input variable is bound to\n421: \t// a sensitive value. This is irrelevant to the validation process, so\n422: \t// we discard the marks now.\n423: \tresult, _ = result.Unmark()\n424: \tstatus := checks.StatusForCtyValue(result)\n425: \n426: \tif status != diags\n434: \t\t}\n435: \n436: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n437: \t\t\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagError,\n438: \t\t\tSummary:     \"Invalid error message\",\n439: \t\t\tDetail: The sequence of these\\n59: \\t// for a given instance might look something like this:\\n60: \\t//\\n61: \\t//          PreProvisionInstance(aws_instance.foo[1], ...)\\n62: \\t//      PreProvisionInstanceStep(aws_instance.foo[1], \\\"file\\\")\\n63: \\t//     PostProvisionInstanceStep(aws_instance.foo[1], \\\"file\\\", nil)\\n64: \\t//      PreProvisionInstanceStep(aws_instance.foo[1], \\\"remote-exec\\\")\\n65: \\t//               ProvisionOutput(aws_instance.foo[1], \\\"remote-exec\\\", \\\"Installing foo...\\\")\\n66: \\t//               ProvisionOutput(aws_instance.foo[1], \\\"remote-exec\\\", \\\"Configuring bar...\\\")\\n67: \\t//     PostProvisionInstanceStep(aws_instance.foo[1], \\\"remote-exec\\\", nil)\\n68: \\t//         PostProvisionInstance(aws_instance.foo[1], ...)\\n69: \\t//\\n70: \\t// ProvisionOutput is called with output sent back by the provisioners.\\n71: \\t// This will be called multiple times as output comes in, with each call\\n72: \\t// representing one line of output. HookResourceIdentity, action plans.Action, opErr error) (HookAction, error)\\n105: \\n106: \\t// Stopping is called if an external signal requests that Terraform\\n107: \\t// gracefully abort an operation in progress.\\n108: \\t//\\n109: \\t// This notification might suggest that the user wants Terraform to exit\\n110: \\t// ASAP and in that case it's possible that if Terraform runs for too much\\n111: \\t// longer then it'll get killed un-gracefully, and so this hook could be\\n112: \\t// an opportunity to persist any transient data that would be lost under\\n113: \\t// a subsequent \\t\\\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/states\\\"\\n13: )\\n14: \\n15: // HookAction is an enum of actions that can be taken as a result of a hook\\n16: // callback. This allows you to modify the behavior of Terraform at runtime.\\n17: type HookAction byte\\n18: \\n19: const (\\n20: \\t// HookActionContinue continues with processing as usual.\\n21: \\tHookActionContinue HookAction = iota\\n22: \\n23: \\t// HookActionHalt halts immediately: no more hooks are processed\\n24: \\t// and the action that Terraform was about to take is cancelled.\\n25: \\tHookActionHalt\\n26: )\\n27: \\n28: // HookResourceIdentity is passed to Hook interface methods to fully identify\\n29: // the resource instance being operated on. If you only want to implement\\n40: // some hook points, but not all (which is the likely case), then embed the\\n41: // NilHook into your struct, which implements all of the interface but does\\n42: // nothing. Then, override only the functions you want to implement.\\n43: type Hook interface {\\n44: \\t// PreApply and PostApply are called before and after an action for a\\n45: \\t// single instance is applied. The error argument in PostApply is the\\n46: \\t// error, if any, that was returned from the provider Apply call itself.\\n47: \\tPreApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, action plans.Action, priorState, plannedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\\n48: \\tPostApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, newState cty.Value, err error) (HookAction, error)\\n49: \\n50: \\t// PreDiff and PostDiff are called before and after a provider is given\\n51: \\t// the opportunity to customize the proposed new state to produce the\\n52: \\t// planned new state.\\n53: \\tPreDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, priorState, proposedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\\n54: \\tPostDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, action plans.Action, priorState, plannedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\\n55: \\n56: \\t// The provisioning hooks signal both the overall start end end of\\n57: \\t// provisioning for a particular instance and of each of the individual\\n58: \\t// configured provisioners for each instance. The sequence of these\\n59: \\t// for a given instance might look something like this:\\n60: \\t//\\n61: \\t//          PreProvisionInstance(aws_instance.foo[1], ...)\\n62: \\t//      PreProvisionInstanceStep(aws_instance.foo[1], \\\"file\\\")\\n63: \\t//     PostProvisionInstanceStep(aws_instance.foo[1], \\\"file\\\", nil)\\n64: \\t//      PreProvisionInstanceStep(aws_instance.foo[1], \\\"remote-exec\\\")\\n65: \\t//               ProvisionOutput(aws_instance.foo[1], \\\"remote-exec\\\", \\\"Installing foo...\\\")\\n66: \\t//               ProvisionOutput(aws_instance.foo[1], \\\"remote-exec\\\", \\\"Configuring bar...\\\")\\n67: \\t//     PostProvisionInstanceStep(aws_instance.foo[1], \\\"remote-exec\\\", nil)\\n68: \\t//         PostProvisionInstance(aws_instance.foo[1], ...)\\n69: \\t//\\n70: \\t// ProvisionOutput is called with output sent back by the provisioners.\\n71: \\t// This will be called multiple times as output comes in, with each call\\n72: \\t// representing one line of output.
